 100: export async function loadBundle(runId: string): Promise<LoadedBundle | null> {
 101:   // typeof guard (not `!relPath`): runId could be an Object.prototype name
 102:   // (toString / __proto__ / constructor) → KNOWN_FIXTURES[runId] returns a
 103:   // function/object → path.join would throw before the try → user-triggerable
 104:   // 500. A non-string lookup → null → BundlePendingCta. (Codex iter-2 P1.)
 105:   const relPath = KNOWN_FIXTURES[runId];
 106:   if (typeof relPath !== "string") return null;
 107:   const dir = path.join(FIXTURE_ROOT, relPath);
 108: 
 109:   try {
 110:     const manifestRaw = await fs.readFile(
 111:       path.join(dir, "manifest.yaml"),
 112:       "utf-8",
 113:     );
 114:     const manifest = parseManifest(manifestRaw);
 115: 
 116:     const scopeDecision = await readJson(dir, manifest, "scope_decision");
 117:     const evidencePool = await readJson(dir, manifest, "evidence_pool");
 118:     const verifiedReport = (await readJson(
 119:       dir,
 120:       manifest,
 121:       "verified_report",
 122:     )) as VerifiedReportShape;
 123: 
 124:     // metadata.json is selected by EXPLICIT PATH per the v1.0 freeze;
 125:     // multiple files may carry content_type=metadata (e.g. REVIEWER_README.md
 126:     // also flagged metadata in the active producer).
 127:     const metadataEntry = manifest.files.find(
 128:       (f) => f.content_type === "metadata" && f.path === "metadata.json",
 129:     );
 130:     if (!metadataEntry) {
 131:       throw new Error(
 132:         `bundle ${runId}: manifest has no entry with path=metadata.json and content_type=metadata`,
 133:       );
 134:     }
 135:     const metadata = JSON.parse(
 136:       await fs.readFile(path.join(dir, "metadata.json"), "utf-8"),
 137:     ) as BundleMetadata;
 138: 
 139:     const reasoningTraceEntry = manifest.files.find(
 140:       (f) => f.content_type === "reasoning_trace",
 141:     );
 142:     const reasoningTrace = reasoningTraceEntry
 143:       ? parseReasoningTraceJsonl(
 144:           await fs.readFile(path.join(dir, reasoningTraceEntry.path), "utf-8"),
 145:         )
 146:       : [];
 147: 
 148:     const sources: Record<string, string> = {};
 149:     for (const entry of manifest.files) {
 150:       if (entry.content_type !== "source_snapshot") continue;
 151:       sources[entry.path] = await fs.readFile(
 152:         path.join(dir, entry.path),
 153:         "utf-8",
 154:       );
 155:     }
 156: 
 157:     // Signature state (tri-valued per I-ux-001a). The boolean check this
 158:     // replaces could call a non-empty placeholder `.asc` "signed". This now
 159:     // requires an actual `gpg --verify` PASS against the shipped trust root
 160:     // in an isolated keyring (so the host's default keyring cannot satisfy
 161:     // the check) AND a fingerprint match to the pinned canonical key
 162:     // (state/polaris_gpg_keyid.txt).
 163:     const { verifyBundleSignature } = await import("./gpg_verify_bundle");
 164:     const sig = await verifyBundleSignature(dir);
 165: 
 166:     return {
 167:       runId,
 168:       manifest,
 169:       scopeDecision,
 170:       evidencePool,
 171:       verifiedReport,
 172:       metadata,
 173:       reasoningTrace,
 174:       sources,
 175:       signatureState: sig.state,
 176:       signatureKeyFingerprint: sig.fingerprint,
 177:     };
 178:   } catch (err) {
 179:     // Graceful: a missing/unreadable/malformed bundle renders the pending
 180:     // state (BundlePendingCta), NEVER a 500. (#789 P0 — the centerpiece must
 181:     // not crash the page.)
 182:     console.error(`[inspector] bundle load failed for ${runId}:`, err);
 183:     return null;
 184:   }
 185: }
 186: 
 187: async function readJson(
 188:   dir: string,
 189:   manifest: BundleManifest,
 190:   contentType: "scope_decision" | "evidence_pool" | "verified_report",
 191: ): Promise<unknown> {
 192:   const entry = manifest.files.find((f) => f.content_type === contentType);
 193:   if (!entry) {
 194:     throw new Error(
 195:       `bundle: manifest has no entry of content_type=${contentType}`,
 196:     );
 197:   }
 198:   const body = await fs.readFile(path.join(dir, entry.path), "utf-8");
 199:   return JSON.parse(body);
 200: }

   1: // I-p2-004 (#743): the SINGLE shared resolver for provenance-token → exact
   2: // source span. Consumed by the citation chip now and by the Proof-Replay
   3: // inspector (#756) — one resolver boundary, no duplicate parsing.
   4: //
   5: // No-synthetic-proof contract (Codex brief iter-2/3): returns quote=null
   6: // (→ honest fallback) unless the bounds are fully valid against the actual
   7: // source body. NEVER a silently-clamped slice (that would be synthetic proof).
   8: 
   9: import { parseProvenanceToken } from "@/lib/provenance_tokens";
  10: 
  11: export interface EvidenceSource {
  12:   source_id: string;
  13:   full_text?: string | null;
  14:   snippet?: string | null;
  15:   title?: string | null;
  16:   url?: string | null;
  17:   tier?: string | number | null;
  18: }
  19: 
  20: export interface ResolvedSpan {
  21:   raw: string;
  22:   sourceId: string;
  23:   source: EvidenceSource | null;
  24:   start: number;
  25:   end: number;
  26:   /** The EXACT cited passage `full_text[start:end]`, or null when unresolved
  27:    * (missing source / no full_text / out-of-range bounds) — never clamped. */
  28:   quote: string | null;
  29: }
  30: 
  31: function sourcesOf(evidencePool: unknown): EvidenceSource[] {
  32:   const s = (evidencePool as { sources?: unknown } | null)?.sources;
  33:   return Array.isArray(s) ? (s as EvidenceSource[]) : [];
  34: }
  35: 
  36: /** A cited span rendered WITH its real surrounding source context so it reads
  37:  * naturally, while the EXACT cited passage stays auditable. `span` is exactly
  38:  * `full_text[start:end]` (unchanged — faithful); `before`/`after` are real
  39:  * adjacent source text snapped to word boundaries; the ellipsis flags signal
  40:  * the context is a window, not the whole body. No synthetic text is introduced. */
  41: export interface SpanInContext {
  42:   before: string;
  43:   span: string;
  44:   after: string;
  45:   leadingEllipsis: boolean;
  46:   trailingEllipsis: boolean;
  47: }
  48: 
  49: /** I-p2-038 (#821): build a word-boundary-snapped context window around an exact
  50:  * cited span so the proof reads naturally (the raw span often starts mid-token).
  51:  * Returns null when the span itself can't be sliced from `fullText`. */
  52: export function spanInContext(
  53:   fullText: string | null | undefined,
  54:   start: number,
  55:   end: number,
  56:   window = 90,
  57: ): SpanInContext | null {
  58:   if (
  59:     typeof fullText !== "string" ||
  60:     start < 0 ||
  61:     end > fullText.length ||
  62:     start > end
  63:   ) {
  64:     return null;
  65:   }
  66:   const span = fullText.slice(start, end);
  67:   // Expand left to a word boundary (so `before` doesn't itself start mid-word).
  68:   let ctxStart = Math.max(0, start - window);
  69:   if (ctxStart > 0) {
  70:     const sp = fullText.indexOf(" ", ctxStart);
  71:     if (sp !== -1 && sp < start) ctxStart = sp + 1;
  72:   }
  73:   // Expand right to a word boundary.
  74:   let ctxEnd = Math.min(fullText.length, end + window);
  75:   if (ctxEnd < fullText.length) {
  76:     const sp = fullText.lastIndexOf(" ", ctxEnd);
  77:     if (sp !== -1 && sp > end) ctxEnd = sp;
  78:   }
  79:   return {
  80:     before: fullText.slice(ctxStart, start),
  81:     span,
  82:     after: fullText.slice(end, ctxEnd),
  83:     leadingEllipsis: ctxStart > 0,
  84:     trailingEllipsis: ctxEnd < fullText.length,
  85:   };
  86: }
  87: 
  88: /** Resolve a `[#ev:<id>:<start>-<end>]` token against the evidence pool.
  89:  * Returns null if the token itself is malformed; otherwise a ResolvedSpan
  90:  * whose `quote` is null unless every bound is valid against the real body. */
  91: export function resolveSpan(
  92:   token: string,
  93:   evidencePool: unknown,
  94: ): ResolvedSpan | null {
  95:   const parsed = parseProvenanceToken(token);
  96:   if (!parsed) return null;
  97:   // sources is an ARRAY → look up by source_id (never index).
  98:   const source =
  99:     sourcesOf(evidencePool).find((s) => s?.source_id === parsed.source_id) ??
 100:     null;
 101:   const body = source?.full_text ?? null; // exact span only from full_text
 102:   let quote: string | null = null;
 103:   if (
 104:     typeof body === "string" &&
 105:     body.length > 0 &&
 106:     parsed.start >= 0 &&
 107:     parsed.end <= body.length &&
 108:     parsed.start <= parsed.end
 109:   ) {
 110:     quote = body.slice(parsed.start, parsed.end);
 111:   }
 112:   return {
 113:     raw: token,
 114:     sourceId: parsed.source_id,
 115:     source,
 116:     start: parsed.start,
 117:     end: parsed.end,
 118:     quote,
 119:   };
 120: }

   3: // LAW-II "no fake working" gate. Previously the loader marked
   4: // signaturePresent=true on any non-empty manifest.yaml.asc, so a placeholder
   5: // `.asc` would render as "Signed bundle." This module replaces that with a
   6: // real `gpg --verify` against the SHIPPED trust-root pubkey
   7: // (docs/carney_handover/polaris_demo_pubkey.asc) in an ISOLATED temporary
   8: // GNUPGHOME (so the host's default keyring cannot satisfy verification), and
   9: // asserts the signing-key fingerprint matches the pinned canonical key
  10: // (state/polaris_gpg_keyid.txt).
  11: //
  12: // Returns `gpg_verified` only on full pass; `present_unverified` if the file
  13: // exists but verification fails for any reason; `missing` otherwise.
  14: 
  15: import { execFile, spawn } from "node:child_process";
  16: import { promises as fs } from "node:fs";
  17: import os from "node:os";
  18: import path from "node:path";
  19: import { promisify } from "node:util";
  20: 
  21: const execFileAsync = promisify(execFile);
  22: 
  23: // I-ux-001a: bake the trust root + pinned fingerprint as constants instead of
  24: // reading from disk. Two wins: (1) the prior CWD walk-up from Next.js cwd=web/
  25: // is gone (Codex iter-1 P1 root cause), (2) the production Docker (build
  26: // context=./web) no longer needs to ship docs/ or state/ files outside its
  27: // context. Both values are PUBLIC by design per docs/carney_secret_inventory.md
  28: // #1 ("Public key may stay published"). Rotation = update both constants and
  29: // the corresponding source files + redeploy.
  30: //
  31: // IMPORTANT (Codex iter-3 P1): TRUST_ROOT_ARMORED is BASE64-encoded so we never
  32: // transcribe multi-line ASCII-armored text by hand again. The earlier hand-
  33: // copied version had a 4-byte transcription error → wrong fingerprint → prod
  34: // would always degrade to present_unverified. The bytes below are
  35: // `base64(file_contents(docs/carney_handover/polaris_demo_pubkey.asc))`.
  36: // `tests/scripts/test_trust_root_consts.py` asserts both constants exactly
  37: // match the shipped source files + that the dearmored bytes produce the
  38: // pinned fingerprint, so this regression cannot recur silently.
  39: const PINNED_FP = "FB221FA8ED185F8E3F76F7E6F6F31CEDFF490C02";
  40: const TRUST_ROOT_BASE64 =
  41:   "LS0tLS1CRUdJTiBQR1AgUFVCTElDIEtFWSBCTE9DSy0tLS0tDQoNCm1ETUVhZ1Zrd2hZSkt3WUJCQUhhUnc4QkFRZEFPMlFBNEpyT1YreThnc21NRjN2SFgzY0svQVhYVTRLbTZpSW8NClpRT2dWM2EwU0ZCUFRFRlNTVk1nUTJGeWJtVjVJRVJsYlc4Z0tFTmhjbTVsZVNCa1pXMXZJR0oxYm1Sc1pTQnoNCmFXZHVhVzVuS1NBOGMybG5ibWx1WjBCd2IyeGhjbWx6TG14dlkyRnNQb2laQkJNV0NnQkJGaUVFK3lJZnFPMFkNClg0NC9kdmZtOXZNYzdmOUpEQUlGQW1vRlpNSUNHd01GQ1FIaE00QUZDd2tJQndJQ0lnSUdGUW9KQ0FzQ0JCWUMNCkF3RUNIZ2NDRjRBQUNna1E5dk1jN2Y5SkRBS0dyd0VBbnF3Rm5HeFdkTW4rUzJycHptbkdRTU10KzFrZGFMM0cNCmhSRVVXM1M3ZUtnQkFPZHpqL2s4bVBvV1VxRXFCa0MvSzhvbHZBcWxLR0RJeGNSSW5SNlhHVkFEDQo9bUFneA0KLS0tLS1FTkQgUEdQIFBVQkxJQyBLRVkgQkxPQ0stLS0tLQ0K";
  42: 
  43: export interface SignatureVerifyResult {
  44:   state: "missing" | "present_unverified" | "gpg_verified";
  45:   /** Hex fingerprint of the signing key when state=gpg_verified. */
  46:   fingerprint?: string;
  47: }
  48: 
  49: export async function verifyBundleSignature(
  50:   bundleDir: string,
  51: ): Promise<SignatureVerifyResult> {
  52:   const ascPath = path.join(bundleDir, "manifest.yaml.asc");
  53:   const manifestPath = path.join(bundleDir, "manifest.yaml");
  54: 
  55:   // 1. presence + non-empty
  56:   try {
  57:     const stat = await fs.stat(ascPath);
  58:     if (!stat.isFile() || stat.size === 0) return { state: "missing" };
  59:   } catch {
  60:     return { state: "missing" };
  61:   }
  62: 
  63:   // 2. Verify with `gpgv` against a freshly-dearmored binary keyring built
  64:   //    ONLY from the baked-in trust root. gpgv is the dedicated verify-only
  65:   //    tool: no gpg-agent spawn, no keyboxd, no host gpg.conf. The keyring
  66:   //    is built fresh each request so the only key gpgv can trust is the
  67:   //    one we pin. Production Docker installs gnupg (apk) so gpg+gpgv are
  68:   //    available; if not, the spawn promise rejects → present_unverified
  69:   //    (Codex iter-2 P1: controlled downgrade, no thrown process error).
  70:   let tmpDir: string | null = null;
  71:   try {
  72:     tmpDir = await fs.mkdtemp(path.join(os.tmpdir(), "polaris-gpgv-"));
  73:     const keyringPath = path.join(tmpDir, "trust.gpg");
  74:     const armored = Buffer.from(TRUST_ROOT_BASE64, "base64");
  75:     // Dearmor: write the armored pubkey to stdin, capture binary stdout.
  76:     // Promise wrapped manually to catch spawn errors (ENOENT etc) as a
  77:     // controlled downgrade rather than an unhandled process throw.
  78:     // I-ux-001a Codex iter-3 fix path + iter-4 ESLint fix: top-level `spawn`
  79:     // import (no `require()` — forbidden by @typescript-eslint/no-require-imports).
  80:     // The Promise wrapping catches spawn errors as a controlled downgrade.
  81:     const de = await new Promise<{ ok: boolean; bin?: Buffer }>((resolve) => {
  82:       let cp;
  83:       try {
  84:         cp = spawn("gpg", ["--no-options", "--batch", "--dearmor"]);
  85:       } catch {
  86:         return resolve({ ok: false });
  87:       }
  88:       const chunks: Buffer[] = [];
  89:       cp.stdout.on("data", (d: Buffer) => chunks.push(d));
  90:       cp.on("error", () => resolve({ ok: false })); // gpg missing → downgrade
  91:       cp.on("close", (code: number | null) =>
  92:         resolve({ ok: code === 0, bin: code === 0 ? Buffer.concat(chunks) : undefined }),
  93:       );
  94:       cp.stdin.on("error", () => resolve({ ok: false }));
  95:       cp.stdin.write(armored);
  96:       cp.stdin.end();
  97:     });
  98:     if (!de.ok || !de.bin) return { state: "present_unverified" };
  99:     await fs.writeFile(keyringPath, de.bin);
 100: 
 101:     // MSYS gpgv mangles absolute Windows paths in --keyring (prepends ~/.gnupg/
 102:     // to anything with a colon). Workaround: cwd=tmpDir + relative keyring.
 103:     // execFile's promisified form rejects on spawn error → caught below.
 104:     const { stdout, stderr } = await execFileAsync("gpgv", [
 105:       "--keyring", "./trust.gpg", "--status-fd", "1",
 106:       path.resolve(ascPath), path.resolve(manifestPath),
 107:     ], { cwd: tmpDir });
 108:     const m = (stdout + stderr).match(/VALIDSIG\s+([0-9A-F]{40})\b/i);
 109:     const fp = m ? m[1].toUpperCase() : null;
 110:     if (!fp) return { state: "present_unverified" };
 111:     if (fp !== PINNED_FP) return { state: "present_unverified" };
 112:     return { state: "gpg_verified", fingerprint: fp };
 113:   } catch {
 114:     return { state: "present_unverified" };
 115:   } finally {
 116:     if (tmpDir) await fs.rm(tmpDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {});
 117:   }
 118: }

   3: // Asserts zero serious/critical axe violations on the marketing-auth hero

  13: 
  14: const WCAG_TAGS = ["wcag2a", "wcag2aa", "wcag21a", "wcag21aa", "wcag22aa"];
  15: 
  16: function critical_or_serious(v: { impact?: string | null }) {
  17:   return v.impact === "serious" || v.impact === "critical";
  18: }
  19: 
  20: test.describe("I-ux-001c · Home v6 axe WCAG 2.2 AA", () => {
  21:   test("desktop 1440x900 — zero serious/critical axe violations", async ({
  22:     page,
  23:   }) => {
  24:     await page.setViewportSize({ width: 1440, height: 900 });
  25:     await page.goto("/", { waitUntil: "networkidle" });
  26:     await expect(page.getByTestId("home-h1")).toBeVisible();
  27:     await expect(page.getByTestId("proof-as-cta")).toBeVisible();
  28: 
  29:     const results = await new AxeBuilder({ page })
  30:       .withTags(WCAG_TAGS)
  31:       .analyze();
  32:     // Codex diff iter-1 P2-003: the brief calls for "axe WCAG 2.2 AA"
  33:     // strictness; previously this only filtered serious+critical. We now
  34:     // assert ZERO violations across all impacts (minor/moderate/serious/
  35:     // critical). The serious/critical breakdown is retained in the
  36:     // diagnostic message so a regression localizes immediately.
  37:     const blockers = results.violations.filter(critical_or_serious);
  38:     expect(
  39:       results.violations,
  40:       `serious/critical: ${JSON.stringify(blockers, null, 2)}\n\nall: ${JSON.stringify(results.violations, null, 2)}`,

   1: import { expect, test } from "@playwright/test";
   2: 
   3: /**
   4:  * I-f1-003 — Live template suggestion as user types.
   5:  *
   6:  * Validates the debounced + scored search inside the command palette:
   7:  *  - "tirzepatide" (synonym) → exactly one visible item: clinical.
   8:  *  - "BPEI" (no match) → empty list (zero false-positives).
   9:  *  - "tirzepatide" + Enter → /intake?template=clinical via scoring path.
  10:  *
  11:  * Each test waits for header-sign-in-link visible after networkidle to
  12:  * prove client shell hydration; then opens palette via Ctrl+K.
  13:  */
  14: 
  15: const SUGGEST_BUDGET_MS = 250; // 150ms debounce + 100ms render budget
  16: 
  17: test.describe("Command palette suggest — I-f1-003", () => {
  18:   test("synonym 'tirzepatide' yields exactly one item: clinical", async ({
  19:     page,
  20:   }) => {
  21:     await page.goto("/", { waitUntil: "networkidle" });
  22:     await expect(page.getByTestId("header-sign-in-link")).toBeVisible();
  23: 
  24:     await page.keyboard.press("Control+k");
  25:     await expect(page.getByTestId("command-palette")).toBeVisible();
  26: 
  27:     // Empty palette opens with all 8 templates visible (initial state).
  28:     const items = page.locator('[data-testid^="palette-item-"]');
  29:     await expect(items).toHaveCount(8);
  30: 
  31:     await page.getByTestId("command-palette-input").fill("tirzepatide");
  32:     // Post-debounce post-scoring: synonym map fires and only clinical
  33:     // survives the filter. Plain substring filter would yield 0 items
  34:     // (no template name/summary contains "tirzepatide"), so this
  35:     // assertion proves scoring + synonym map ran.
  36:     await expect(items).toHaveCount(1, { timeout: SUGGEST_BUDGET_MS + 100 });
  37:     await expect(page.getByTestId("palette-item-clinical")).toBeVisible();
  38:   });
  39: 
  40:   test("'BPEI' yields zero items (no false-positive)", async ({ page }) => {
  41:     await page.goto("/", { waitUntil: "networkidle" });

  52:   });

 succeeded in 989ms:
codex
The shell policy rejected the PowerShell background-server form, so I’m switching to a single Node harness that starts Next as a child process, runs the focused Chromium tests, and tears the child down in-process. That keeps the resource ownership tighter.
exec
"C:\\Program Files\\PowerShell\\7\\pwsh.exe" -Command "@'
const { spawn } = require('node:child_process');
const http = require('node:http');
const path = require('node:path');

const cwd = path.join(process.cwd(), 'web');
const nextBin = path.join(cwd, 'node_modules', 'next', 'dist', 'bin', 'next');
const pwCli = path.join(cwd, 'node_modules', '@playwright', 'test', 'cli.js');
const baseURL = 'http://127.0.0.1:3738';

function waitForServer(url, timeoutMs = 90000) {
  const deadline = Date.now() + timeoutMs;
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const tick = () => {
      const req = http.get(url, (res) => {
        res.resume();
        if (res.statusCode >= 200 && res.statusCode < 500) resolve();
        else retry();
      });
      req.setTimeout(2000, () => { req.destroy(); retry(); });
      req.on('error', retry);
    };
    const retry = () => {
      if (Date.now() > deadline) reject(new Error('Next dev server did not become ready'));
      else setTimeout(tick, 1000);
    };
    tick();
  });
}

function runChild(cmd, args, opts = {}) {
  return new Promise((resolve) => {
    const child = spawn(cmd, args, { cwd, stdio: 'inherit', ...opts });
    child.on('exit', (code, signal) => resolve({ code, signal }));
  });
}

(async () => {
  const server = spawn(process.execPath, [nextBin, 'dev', '--hostname', '127.0.0.1', '--port', '3738'], {
    cwd,
    stdio: ['ignore', 'pipe', 'pipe'],
    env: { ...process.env, PORT: '3738' },
  });
  const lines = [];
  const capture = (chunk) => {
    const text = chunk.toString();
    process.stdout.write(text);
    lines.push(...text.split(/\\r?\\n/));
    while (lines.length > 80) lines.shift();
  };
  server.stdout.on('data', capture);
  server.stderr.on('data', capture);

  let exitCode = 1;
  try {
    await waitForServer(baseURL);
    const result = await runChild(process.execPath, [
      pwCli,
      'test',
      'tests/e2e/home_proof_as_cta.spec.ts',
      'tests/e2e/command_palette.spec.ts',
      'tests/e2e/command_palette_suggest.spec.ts',
      'tests/e2e/command_palette_adversarial.spec.ts',
      '--project=chromium',
    ], { env: { ...process.env, SCREENSHOT_BASE_URL: baseURL } });
    exitCode = result.code ?? 1;
  } catch (err) {
    console.error(err && err.stack ? err.stack : err);
    console.error('--- next output tail ---');
    console.error(lines.join('\\n'));
  } finally {
    if ("'!server.killed) server.kill('"'SIGTERM');
    setTimeout(() => { if ("'!server.killed) server.kill('"'SIGKILL'); }, 3000).unref();
  }
  process.exit(exitCode);
})();
